## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Task: Document Cilium eBPF Map API

## Objective

Generate comprehensive API reference documentation for Cilium's eBPF map API in the `pkg/bpf` package. The documentation should serve as a complete reference for developers working with eBPF maps in Cilium.

## Scope

Focus on the Go wrappers in `pkg/bpf` that provide user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps. Document:

1. **Core Map Type and Creation**
   - `Map` struct and its primary methods
   - Map creation functions (`NewMap`, `OpenMap`, `OpenOrCreate`)
   - Map lifecycle operations (Open, Create, Close, Recreate)

2. **CRUD Operations**
   - Lookup, Update, Delete operations
   - Batch operations (BatchLookup, DeleteAll)
   - Per-CPU map operations
   - Locked operations (DeleteLocked)

3. **Iteration and Dumping**
   - Dump methods and callbacks
   - BatchIterator type and usage
   - DumpStats for tracking iteration

4. **Pinning and Persistence**
   - Pin/Unpin operations
   - BPF filesystem paths (BPFFSRoot, CiliumPath, MapPath)
   - Map persistence behavior

5. **Key/Value Interfaces**
   - MapKey, MapValue, MapPerCPUValue interfaces
   - EndpointKey as concrete example

6. **Event System**
   - Event types (MapUpdate, MapDelete)
   - DumpAndSubscribe for event streaming
   - Event callbacks and handles

7. **Collection Loading**
   - LoadCollection and LoadAndAssign functions
   - CollectionOptions

## Requirements

Your documentation must include:

1. **API Method Signatures**: Complete signatures with parameter types and return values
2. **Behavioral Semantics**:
   - When maps are pinned vs unpinned
   - Difference between Create() and CreateUnpinned()
   - OpenOrCreate() behavior on existing maps
   - How deletion works within DumpCallback (requires DeleteLocked)
   - Event subscription lifecycle
   - Batch iterator retry behavior on ENOSPC
3. **Usage Examples**: Code snippets showing:
   - Basic map creation and CRUD
   - Iteration with BatchIterator
   - Event subscription and cleanup
   - Pinning and unpinning maps
   - Real-world patterns from Cilium internals
4. **Documentation Structure**: Organize clearly with sections for each category above

## Deliverable

Write your documentation to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format.

## Constraints

- Do NOT include file paths or specific implementation locations in the documentation
- Focus on API contracts and behavior, not internal implementation details
- Include enough behavioral detail that users can correctly use the API without reading source code
- Provide accurate examples that would compile and work correctly

## Summary

The documentation covers all requested areas with detailed API signatures, behavioral semantics, and practical examples:

### Key Sections:

1. **Core Map Type and Creation** - `NewMap`, `OpenMap`, `OpenOrCreate`, `CreateUnpinned`, `Create`, `Recreate`, `Open`, `Close`

3. **Iteration and Dumping** - Multiple strategies including:
   - Callback-based: `DumpWithCallback`, `DumpWithCallbackIfExists`
   - Reliable: `DumpReliablyWithCallback` with backtracking support
   - Batch API: `BatchIterator` with automatic retry on ENOSPC

4. **Batch Operations** - `BatchLookup`, `BatchCount`, and `BatchIterator` with examples of handling LRU hash map buffer sizing

5. **Pinning and Persistence** - Complete coverage of `Pin`, `Unpin`, BPF filesystem paths, and map persistence behavior

6. **Key/Value Interfaces** - Full documentation of `MapKey`, `MapValue`, and `MapPerCPUValue` with concrete examples

7. **Event System** - Event types, subscription model, TTL-based garbage collection, and usage examples

8. **Collection Loading** - `LoadAndAssign`, `LoadCollection`, `CollectionOptions`, and pin replacement semantics

9. **Additional Coverage** - Cache management, pressure metrics, error handling, best practices, and utility functions

- When `DeleteLocked` must be used vs regular `Delete`

With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\\n704: // retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\\n705: //\\n706: // To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\\n707: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\\n708: \\tif cb == nil {\\n709: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n710: \\t}\\n711: \\n712: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n713: \\t\\treturn err\\n714: \\t}\\n715: \\n716: \\tm.lock.RLock()\\n717: \\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\\n718: \\n719: \\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\\n720: \\tmk := m.key.New()\\n721: \\tmv := m.value.New()\\n722: \\n723: \\ti := m.m.Iterate()\\n724: \\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\\n725: \\t\\tcb(mk, mv)\\n726: \\n727: \\t\\tmk = m.key.New()\\n728: \\t\\tmv = m.value.New()\\n729: \\t}\\n730: \\n731: \\treturn i.Err()\\n732: }\\n733: \\n734: // DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\\n735: // the slice of all values from all CPUs.\\n736: type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\\n737: \\n738: // DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\\n739: // DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\\n740: // from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\\n741: // to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\\n742: func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\\n743: \\tif cb == nil {\\n744: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n745: \\t}\\n746: \\n747: \\tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\\n748: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\\\", m.name)\\n749: \\t}\\n750: \\n751: \\tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\\n752: \\tif !ok {\\n753: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\\\", m.name)\\n754: \\t}\\n755: \\n756: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n757: \\t\\treturn err\\n758: \\t}\\n759: \\n760: \\tm.lock.RLock()\\n761: \\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\\n762: \\n763: \\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\\n764: \\tmk := m.key.New()\\n765: \\tmv := v.NewSlice()\\n766: \\n767: \\ti := m.m.Iterate()\\n768: \\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\\n769: \\t\\tcb(mk, mv)\\n770: \\n771: \\t\\tmk = m.key.New()\\n772: \\t\\tmv = v.NewSlice()\\n773: \\t}\\n774: \\n775: \\treturn i.Err()\\n776: }\\n777: \\n778: // DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\\n779: // if the given map does not exist.\\n780: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\\n781: \\tfound, err := m.exist()\\n782: \\tif err != nil {\\n783: \\t\\treturn err\\n784: \\t}\\n785: \\n786: \\tif found {\\n787: \\t\\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\\n788: \\t}\\n789: \\n790: \\treturn nil\\n791: }\\n792: \\n793: // DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\\n794: // additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\\n795: // element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\\n796: // can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\\n797: // In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\\n798: // the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\\n799: //\\n800: // The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\\n801: // object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\\n802: // not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\\n803: func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\\n804: \\tif cb == nil {\\n805: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n806: \\t}\\n807: \\n808: \\tif stats == nil {\\n809: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"stats is nil\\\")\\n810: \\t}\\n811: \\n812: \\tvar (\\n813: \\t\\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\\n814: \\t\\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\\n815: \\t\\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\\n816: \\t\\tvalue      = m.value.New()\\n817: \\n818: \\t\\tprevKeyValid = false\\n819: \\t)\\n820: \\n821: \\tstats.start()\\n822: \\tdefer stats.finish()\\n823: \\n824: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n825: \\t\\treturn err\\n826: \\t}\\n827: \\n828: \\t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\\n829: \\t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\\n830: \\t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\\n831: \\tm.lock.Lock()\\n832: \\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\\n833: \\tif m.m == nil {\\n834: \\t\\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\\n835: \\t\\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\\n836: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"map is closed\\\")\\n837: \\t}\\n838: \\n839: \\t// Get the first map key.\\n840: \\tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\\n841: \\t\\tstats.Lookup = 1\\n842: \\t\\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\\n843: \\t\\t\\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\\n844: \\t\\t\\tstats.Completed = true\\n845: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n846: \\t\\t}\\n847: \\t}\\n848: \\n849: \\t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\\n850: \\t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\\n851: \\t// updated while being iterated)\\n852: \\tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\\n853: \\n854: \\t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\\n855: \\t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\\n856: \\t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\\n857: \\tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\\n858: \\t\\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\\n859: \\t\\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\\n860: \\t\\t//\\n861: \\t\\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\\n862: \\t\\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\\n863: \\t\\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\\n864: \\t\\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\\n865: \\t\\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\\n866: \\n867: \\t\\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\\n868: \\t\\t\\tstats.LookupFailed++\\n869: \\t\\t\\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\\n870: \\t\\t\\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\\n871: \\t\\t\\tif prevKeyValid {\\n872: \\t\\t\\t\\tcurrentKey = prevKey\\n873: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\\n874: \\t\\t\\t\\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\\n875: \\t\\t\\t\\tprevKeyValid = false\\n876: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.KeyFallback++\\n877: \\t\\t\\t} else {\\n878: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\\n879: \\t\\t\\t\\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\\n880: \\t\\t\\t\\t// one, or the first element in the map.\\n881: \\t\\t\\t\\tcurrentKey = nextKey\\n882: \\t\\t\\t\\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\\n883: \\t\\t\\t\\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\\n884: \\t\\t\\t\\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\\n885: \\t\\t\\t\\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\tnextKey = m.key.New()\\n887: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.Interrupted++\\n888: \\t\\t\\t}\\n889: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n890: \\t\\t}\\n891: \\n892: \\t\\tcb(currentKey, value)\\n893: \\n894: \\t\\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\\n895: \\t\\t\\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\\n896: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.Completed = true\\n897: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\\n898: \\t\\t\\t}\\n899: \\t\\t\\treturn nextKeyErr\\n900: \\t\\t}\\n901: \\n902: \\t\\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\\n903: \\t\\tprevKey = currentKey\\n904: \\t\\tcurrentKey = nextKey\\n905: \\t\\tnextKey = m.key.New()\\n906: \\t\\tprevKeyValid = true\\n907: \\t}\\n908: \\n909: \\treturn ErrMaxLookup\\n910: }\\n911: \\n912: // BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\\n913: // of bpf maps.\\n914: type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\\n915: \\tm    *Map\\n916: \\terr  error\\n917: \\tkeys []KT\\n918: \\tvals []VT\\n919: \\n920: \\tchunkSize      int\\n921: \\tmaxDumpRetries uint32\\n922: \\n923: \\t// Iteration stats\\n924: \\tbatchSize int\\n925: \\n926: \\topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\\n927: }\\n928: \\n929: // NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\\n930: // This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling errors\\n931: // when end of map is reached.\\n932: // Following iteration, any unresolved errors encountered when iterating\\n933: // the bpf map can be accessed via the Err() function.\\n934: // The pointer type of KT & VT must implement Map{Key,Value}, respectively.\\n935: //\\n936: // Subsequent iterations via IterateAll reset all internal state and begin\\n937: // iteration over.\\n938: //\\n939: // Example usage:\\n940: //\\n941: //\\tm := NewMap(\\\"cilium_test\\\",\\n942: //\\t\\tebpf.Hash,\\n943: //\\t\\t&TestKey{}, \\t// *TestKey implements MapKey.\\n944: //\\t\\t&TestValue{}, }\\n1028: \\n1029: // CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\\n1030: // iterator.\\n1031: func CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP \\treturn c, iter.Err()\\n1037: }\\n1038: \\n1039: func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\\n1040: \\tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\\n1041: \\tnearest2 := \\tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\\n1059: \\t\\tbreak\\n1060: \\tdefault:\\n1061: \\t\\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\\\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\\\", ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)\\n1099: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\\n1100: \\t\\t\\t\\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map // OpenOrCreate attempts to open the Map, or if it does not yet exist, create\n561: // the Map. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\n704: // retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n705: //\n706: // To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\n707: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\n708: \tif cb == nil {\n709: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n710: \t}\n711: \n712: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n713: \t\treturn err\n714: \t}\n715: \n716: \tm.lock.RLock()\n717: \tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n718: \n719: \t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n720: \tmk := m.key.New()\n721: \tmv := m.value.New()\n722: \n723: \ti := m.m.Iterate()\n724: \tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n725: \t\tcb(mk, mv)\n726: \n727: \t\tmk = m.key.New()\n728: \t\tmv = m.value.New()\n729: \t}\n730: \n731: \treturn i.Err()\n732: }\n733: \n734: // DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\n735: // the slice of all values from all CPUs.\n736: type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n737: \n738: // DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\n739: // DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\n740: // from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\n741: // to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n742: func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\n743: \tif cb == nil {\n744: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n745: \t}\n746: \n747: \tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\n748: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\", m.name)\n749: \t}\n750: \n751: \tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\n752: \tif !ok {\n753: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\", m.name)\n754: \t}\n755: \n756: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n757: \t\treturn err\n758: \t}\n759: \n760: \tm.lock.RLock()\n761: \tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n762: \n763: \t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n764: \tmk := m.key.New()\n765: \tmv := v.NewSlice()\n766: \n767: \ti := m.m.Iterate()\n768: \tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n769: \t\tcb(mk, mv)\n770: \n771: \t\tmk = m.key.New()\n772: \t\tmv = v.NewSlice()\n773: \t}\n774: \n775: \treturn i.Err()\n776: }\n777: \n778: // DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\n779: // if the given map does not exist.\n780: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\n781: \tfound, err := m.exist()\n782: \tif err != nil {\n783: \t\treturn err\n784: \t}\n785: \n786: \tif found {\n787: \t\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \treturn nil\n791: }\n792: \n793: // DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\n794: // additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\n795: // element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\n796: // can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\n797: // In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\n798: // the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\n799: //\n800: // The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\n801: // object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\n802: // not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\n803: func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\n804: \tif cb == nil {\n805: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n806: \t}\n807: \n808: \tif stats == nil {\n809: \t\treturn errors.New(\"stats is nil\")\n810: \t}\n811: \n812: \tvar (\n813: \t\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\n814: \t\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\n815: \t\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\n816: \t\tvalue      = m.value.New()\n817: \n818: \t\tprevKeyValid = false\n819: \t)\n820: \n821: \tstats.start()\n822: \tdefer stats.finish()\n823: \n824: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n825: \t\treturn err\n826: \t}\n827: \n828: \t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\n829: \t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\n830: \t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\n831: \tm.lock.Lock()\n832: \tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n833: \tif m.m == nil {\n834: \t\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\n835: \t\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\n836: \t\treturn errors.New(\"map is closed\")\n837: \t}\n838: \n839: \t// Get the first map key.\n840: \tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\n841: \t\tstats.Lookup = 1\n842: \t\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n843: \t\t\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\n844: \t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n845: \t\t\treturn nil\n846: \t\t}\n847: \t}\n848: \n849: \t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\n850: \t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\n851: \t// updated while being iterated)\n852: \tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\n853: \n854: \t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\n855: \t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\n856: \t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\n857: \tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\n858: \t\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\n859: \t\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\n860: \t\t//\n861: \t\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\n862: \t\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\n863: \t\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\n864: \t\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\n865: \t\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\n866: \n867: \t\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\n868: \t\t\tstats.LookupFailed++\n869: \t\t\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\n870: \t\t\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\n871: \t\t\tif prevKeyValid {\n872: \t\t\t\tcurrentKey = prevKey\n873: \t\t\t\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\n874: \t\t\t\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\n875: \t\t\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n876: \t\t\t\tstats.KeyFallback++\n877: \t\t\t} else {\n878: \t\t\t\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\n879: \t\t\t\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\n880: \t\t\t\t// one, or the first element in the map.\n881: \t\t\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n882: \t\t\t\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\n883: \t\t\t\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\n884: \t\t\t\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\n885: \t\t\t\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\n886: \t\t\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n887: \t\t\t\tstats.Interrupted++\n888: \t\t\t}\n889: \t\t\tcontinue\n890: \t\t}\n891: \n892: \t\tcb(currentKey, value)\n893: \n894: \t\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\n895: \t\t\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n896: \t\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n897: \t\t\t\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\n898: \t\t\t}\n899: \t\t\treturn nextKeyErr\n900: \t\t}\n901: \n902: \t\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\n903: \t\tprevKey = currentKey\n904: \t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n905: \t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n906: \t\tprevKeyValid = true\n907: \t}\n908: \n909: \treturn ErrMaxLookup\n910: }\n911: \n912: // BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\n913: // of bpf maps.\n914: type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n915: \tm    *Map\n916: \terr  error\n917: \tkeys []KT\n918: \tvals []VT\n919: \n920: \tchunkSize      int\n921: \tmaxDumpRetries uint32\n922: \n923: \t// Iteration stats\n924: \tbatchSize int\n925: \n926: \topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\n927: }\n928: \n929: // NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\n930: // This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling errors\n931: // when end of map is reached.\n932: // Following iteration, any unresolved errors encountered when iterating\n933: // the bpf map can be accessed via the Err() function.\n934: // The pointer type of KT & VT must implement Map{Key,Value}, respectively.\n935: //\n936: // Subsequent iterations via IterateAll reset all internal state and begin\n937: // iteration over.\n938: //\n939: // Example usage:\n940: //\n941: //\tm := NewMap(\"cilium_test\",\n942: //\t\tebpf.Hash,\n943: //\t\t&TestKey{}, \t// *TestKey implements MapKey.\n944: //\t\t&TestValue{}, \t// *TestValue implements MapValue.\n945: //\t\tmapSize,\n946: //\t\tBPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n947: //\t)\n948: //\n949: //\titer := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\n950: //\tfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\n951: //\t\t// ...\n952: //\t}\n953: func NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n954: \treturn &BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]{\n955: \t\tm: m,\n956: \t}\n957: }\n958: \n959: // KeyPointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n960: // of a type T is a MapKey.\n961: type KeyPointer[T any] interface {\n962: \tMapKey\n963: \t*T\n964: }\n965: \n966: // ValuePointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n967: // of a type T is a MapValue.\n968: type ValuePointer[T any] interface {\n969: \tMapValue\n970: \t*T\n971: }\n972: \n973: // Err returns errors encountered during the previous iteration when\n974: // IterateAll(...) is called.\n975: //\n976: // If the iterator is reused, the error will be reset,\n977: func (kvs BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error {\n978: \treturn kvs.err\n979: }\n980: \n981: func (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) maxBatchedRetries() int {\n982: \tif bi.maxDumpRetries > 0 {\n983: \t\treturn int(bi.maxDumpRetries)\n984: \t}\n985: \treturn defaultBatchedRetries\n986: }\n987: \n988: const defaultBatchedRetries = 3\n989: \n990: type BatchIteratorOpt[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] func(*BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n991: \n992: // WithEBPFBatchOpts returns a batch iterator option that allows for overriding\n993: // BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH options.\n994: func WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n995: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n996: \t\tin.opts = opts\n997: \t\treturn in\n998: \t}\n999: }\n1000: \n1001: // WithMaxRetries returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the default\n1002: // max batch retries.\n1003: //\n1004: // Unless the starting chunk size is set to be the map size, it is possible for iteration\n1005: // to fail with ENOSPC if the passed allocated chunk array size is not big enough to accommodate\n1006: // a the bpf maps underlying hashmaps bucket size.\n1007: //\n1008: // If this happens, BatchIterator will automatically attempt to double the batch size and\n1009: // retry the iteration from the same place - up to a number of retries.\n1010: func WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1011: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1012: \t\tin.maxDumpRetries = retries\n1013: \t\treturn in\n1014: \t}\n1015: }\n1016: \n1017: // WithStartingChunkSize returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the dynamically\n1018: // chosen starting chunk size.\n1019: func WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1020: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1021: \t\tin.chunkSize = size\n1022: \t\tif in.chunkSize <= 0 {\n1023: \t\t\tin.chunkSize = 8\n1024: \t\t}\n1025: \t\treturn in\n1026: \t}\n1027: }\n1028: \n1029: // CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\n1030: // iterator.\n1031: func CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error) {\n1032: \tc := 0\n1033: \tfor range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n1034: \t\tc++\n1035: \t}\n1036: \treturn c, iter.Err()\n1037: }\n1038: \n1039: func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\n1040: \tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\n1041: \tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\n1042: \treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\n1043: }\n1044: \n1045: // IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\n1046: // using the batched API.\n1047: // In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\n1048: // this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\n1049: // of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\n1050: // If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\n1051: // will be returned via Err().\n1052: //\n1053: // All other errors will result in immediate termination of iterator.\n1054: //\n1055: // If the iteration fails, then the Err() function will return the error that caused the failure.\n1056: func (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP] {\n1057: \tswitch bi.m.Type() {\n1058: \tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\n1059: \t\tbreak\n1060: \tdefault:\n1061: \t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\", bi.m.Type())\n1062: \t\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {}\n1063: \t}\n1064: \n1065: \tbi.chunkSize = startingChunkSize(int(bi.m.MaxEntries()))\n1066: \n1067: \tfor _, not big enough to\n1100: \t\t\t\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map [1]\n1101: \t\t\t\t// Because bucket size, in general, cannot be known, we approximate a good starting\n1102: \t\t\t\t// buffer size from the approximation of how many entries there should be in the map\n1103: \t\t\t\t// before expect to see a hash map collision: sqrt(max_entries * 2)\n1104: \t\t\t\t//\n1105: 24. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference\n\nThis document provides comprehensive reference documentation for Cilium's eBPF map API, focusing on the Go wrappers in the `pkg/bpf` package that provide user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps.\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Core Map Type and Creation](#core-map-type-and-creation)\n2. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n3. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n4. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n5. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n6. [Event System](#event-system)\n7. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n\n---\n\n## Core Map Type and Creation\n\n### Map Struct\n\nThe `Map` struct represents a BPF map in user space. It provides methods to interact with kernel eBPF maps and includes features for caching, events, and persistence.\n\n### Map Creation Functions\n\n#### `NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue, maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map`\n\nCreates a new Map instance with the specified parameters.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: The name of the map (used for pinning)\n- `mapType`: Type of eBPF map (Hash, LRUHash, Array, PerCPUHash, etc.)\n- `mapKey`: A MapKey implementation defining the key structure\n- `mapValue`: A MapValue implementation defining the value structure\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum number of entries the map can hold\n- `flags`: eBPF map creation flags (e.g., `BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`)\n\n**Returns:** A new Map instance in uninitialized state (not yet opened/created)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{}\nvalue := &MyValue{}\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_my_map\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    key,\n    value,\n    10000,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n)\n```\n\n#### `NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue, maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map`\n\nCreates a new Map with an inner map specification. Used for maps-of-maps or maps-of-programs.\n\n**Parameters:** Same as `NewMap`, plus:\n- `innerSpec`: The specification for the inner map\n\n#### `OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)`\n\nOpens an existing pinned map from the filesystem.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `pinPath`: Absolute path to the pinned map file\n- `key`: A MapKey implementation matching the map's key type\n- `value`: A MapValue implementation matching the map's value type\n\n**Returns:** An open Map instance, or an error if the map doesn't exist or is incompatible\n\n**Requirements:**\n- `pinPath` must be an absolute path\n- The pinned map must have compatible key and value sizes\n\n### Map Lifecycle Operations\n\n#### `Open() error`\n\nOpens an already-pinned map on the filesystem. All calls are serialized by internal locking.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns immediately if the map is already open\n- Loads the map from the pinned path\n- Returns error if map does not exist at the pinned path\n\n#### `OpenOrCreate() error`\n\nAttempts to open a pinned map, or creates a new one if it doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If map exists on filesystem: loads it and verifies compatibility\n- If map doesn't exist: creates a new one and pins it\n- If existing map is incompatible (different type, key/value size, etc.): deletes it and creates a new one\n- If map is marked as non-persistent: always recreates (does not attempt to load)\n\n**Important:** Returns immediately if the map is already open.\n\n#### `CreateUnpinned() error`\n\nCreates a new map in the kernel without pinning it to the filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates the map in memory only\n- No persistence across restarts\n- Useful for temporary maps or when persistence is managed externally\n\n#### `Create() error`\n\nCreates or opens the map, then immediately closes it.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Equivalent to calling `OpenOrCreate()` followed by `Close()`\n- Useful for just ensuring the map exists without keeping it open\n\n#### `Recreate() error`\n\nRemoves the pinned map and recreates it from scratch.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes any existing pin at the map's path\n- Creates a fresh map\n- Re-pins the new map\n- Returns error if map is already open\n\n**Use case:** Clearing all map data when an incompatible state is detected\n\n#### `Close() error`\n\nCloses the map and releases kernel resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Closes the underlying eBPF map file descriptor\n- Stops any background error resolver if enabled\n- Does not remove the pinned map from filesystem\n- Safe to call multiple times\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\nAll CRUD operations require the map to be open. They will automatically call `Open()` if needed, except for locked operations which assume `Open()` has been called.\n\n### Read Operations\n\n#### `Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)`\n\nLooks up a single value in the map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to look up\n\n**Returns:** A new instance of the value type, or an error\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns a new MapValue instance for each call\n- Returns `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if key is not found\n- Thread-safe\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nval, err := m.Lookup(&MyKey{ID: 42})\nif err != nil {\n    if errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n        // Key not found\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Write Operations\n\n#### `Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error`\n\nInserts or updates a value in the map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to insert/update\n- `value`: The value to store\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates or updates the entry atomically\n- Thread-safe (serialized by internal lock)\n- If caching is enabled, updates the cache entry\n- If caching is enabled and update fails, schedules error resolver to retry\n- Records update events if event buffer is enabled\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := m.Update(&MyKey{ID: 42}, &MyValue{Data: 100})\n```\n\n### Delete Operations\n\n#### `Delete(key MapKey) error`\n\nDeletes an entry from the map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete\n\n**Returns:** An error if the key doesn't exist or operation fails\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes the entry atomically\n- Thread-safe\n- Returns error if key doesn't exist\n- Updates cache if enabled\n- Records delete event if event buffer is enabled\n\n#### `SilentDelete(key MapKey) (bool, error)`\n\nDeletes an entry from the map, ignoring missing keys.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `key`: The key to delete\n\n**Returns:** (true if deleted, false if not found, error)\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Same as Delete() but returns (false, nil) instead of error if key is not found\n- Useful for cleanup operations where missing entries are acceptable\n\n#### `DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error`\n\nDeletes a map entry when the map lock is already held.\n\n**Important Requirements:**\n- **Must only be called from within a DumpCallback** to avoid deadlocks\n- Assumes `m.lock` is already acquired for writing\n- Used when you need to delete entries while iterating the map\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    if shouldDelete(key) {\n        m.DeleteLocked(key) // Safe because callback holds the lock\n    }\n})\n```\n\n#### `DeleteAll() error`\n\nDeletes all entries from the map by iterating and deleting individually.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Iterates through all entries and deletes each one\n- Updates cache for each deletion\n- Records a single MapDeleteAll event after completion\n- Entries added during iteration may survive the deletion\n- Thread-safe\n\n**Warning:** Not suitable for very large maps as it iterates every entry. For production clearing, consider `ClearAll()` (if events are not needed).\n\n#### `ClearAll() error`\n\nClears all entries by updating them with empty values instead of deleting.\n\n**Restrictions:**\n- Cannot be used if events buffer is enabled\n- Cannot be used if value cache is enabled\n\n**Behavior:**\n- More efficient than DeleteAll for very large maps\n- Does not record events\n- Thread-safe\n\n### Batch Operations\n\n#### `BatchLookup(cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor, keysOut, valuesOut any, opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) (int, error)`\n\nPerforms a batch lookup of multiple entries.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cursor`: Cursor for iteration (persists state across calls)\n- `keysOut`: Pre-allocated slice to receive keys\n- `valuesOut`: Pre-allocated slice to receive values\n- `opts`: Optional batch options\n\n**Returns:** Number of entries read, and error\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Direct wrapper around the underlying eBPF batch lookup\n- More efficient for reading large numbers of entries\n- Returns `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` when end of map is reached\n- May return `unix.ENOSPC` if buffer is too small for LRU hash maps\n\n**Use Case:** Use `BatchIterator` instead for easier iteration with automatic retry logic\n\n#### `BatchCount() (int, error)`\n\nReturns the total number of elements in the map using batch lookup.\n\n**Restrictions:**\n- Only works on Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie maps\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Iterates entire map to count entries\n- Automatically handles ENOSPC by doubling buffer size (up to 3 retries)\n- Returns error if max retries exceeded\n\n### Per-CPU Operations\n\n#### `DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error`\n\nIterates over a per-CPU map, calling the callback for each key with all CPU values.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function receiving key and slice of values from all CPUs\n\n**Type Definition:**\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Only works with per-CPU map types (PerCPUHash, PerCPUArray, LRUCPUHash, PerCPUCGroupStorage)\n- Callback receives a slice of MapValue instances (one per CPU)\n- Thread-safe\n- Value instances are fresh for each callback\n\n**Requirement:** Value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue` interface\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### Callback-Based Iteration\n\n#### `DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error`\n\nIterates over all map entries, calling the callback for each entry.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function receiving key and value\n\n**Type Definition:**\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Iterates using the ebpf-go Iterator\n- Calls callback for each entry\n- Callback receives fresh MapValue instances\n- Thread-safe (read-lock held during iteration)\n\n**Important:** Callbacks should not perform operations that require write access to the map\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := m.DumpWithCallback(func(key, value MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", key, value)\n})\n```\n\n#### `DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error`\n\nLike `DumpWithCallback`, but returns without error if map doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns nil if map doesn't exist\n- Otherwise identical to DumpWithCallback\n\n#### `DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error`\n\nDumps map contents into a Go map, if the map exists.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Converts keys and values to strings using String() method\n- Returns nil if map doesn't exist\n- Returns error if dump fails\n\n#### `Dump(hash map[string][]string) error`\n\nDumps all map entries into a Go map using string representations.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `hash`: Pre-allocated map to receive string-formatted entries\n- Keys are map keys, values are slices of string values\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Iterates entire map using DumpWithCallback\n- Converts keys/values to strings\n- Multiple values for same key are appended to the slice\n- Thread-safe\n\n### Reliable Iteration with Backtracking\n\n#### `DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error`\n\nIterates over the map with support for concurrent modifications during iteration.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function receiving key and value\n- `stats`: DumpStats instance to track iteration metrics\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Handles keys deleted during iteration by backtracking to recently seen keys\n- Handles iteration restart if all keys are deleted during traversal\n- Caps iteration at 4x the maximum map size to prevent infinite loops\n- Holds map lock during iteration (required for callbacks with map operations)\n- Returns `ErrMaxLookup` if iteration limit exceeded\n\n**Thread-Safety:** Holds write lock during iteration - callbacks can perform map operations\n\n**Use Case:** When iterating maps that are actively modified by other goroutines\n\n**DumpStats Fields:**\n- `Started`: Timestamp when iteration started\n- `Finished`: Timestamp when iteration completed\n- `Lookup`: Total number of key lookups\n- `LookupFailed`: Number of failed lookups\n- `KeyFallback`: Times we fell back to previous key\n- `Interrupted`: Times iteration was interrupted\n- `MaxEntries`: Maximum map capacity\n- `Completed`: Whether iteration finished successfully\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb, stats)\nif err == ErrMaxLookup {\n    // Map too volatile, consider alternative approach\n}\nfmt.Printf(\"Completed: %v, Lookups: %d\\n\", stats.Completed, stats.Lookup)\n```\n\n### Batch Iterator\n\n#### `NewBatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]`\n\nCreates a new batch iterator for efficient iteration using the batch API.\n\n**Type Parameters:**\n- `KT`: Key type\n- `VT`: Value type\n- `KP`: Pointer to key type (must implement MapKey)\n- `VP`: Pointer to value type (must implement MapValue)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyKey struct { ID uint32 }\ntype MyValue struct { Data uint32 }\n\n// Implement MapKey and MapValue interfaces\nfunc (k *MyKey) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"key=%d\", k.ID) }\nfunc (k *MyKey) New() MapKey { return &MyKey{} }\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string { return fmt.Sprintf(\"val=%d\", v.Data) }\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() MapValue { return &MyValue{} }\n\n// Create iterator\niter := NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue](m)\n\n// Iterate\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    // k is *MyKey, v is *MyValue\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    // Handle error\n}\n```\n\n#### `BatchIterator.IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]`\n\nReturns an iterator sequence for batch-based iteration.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Automatically determines starting chunk size based on map size\n- Handles ENOSPC by doubling buffer size and retrying (default: 3 retries)\n- Respects context cancellation\n- Returns all key-value pairs as pointers\n- Resets internal state on each call (can be reused)\n\n**Restrictions:**\n- Only works on Hash, LRUHash, and LPMTrie maps\n\n**Options:**\n- `WithEBPFBatchOpts(*ebpf.BatchOptions)`: Override batch options\n- `WithMaxRetries(uint32)`: Set max retries for ENOSPC (default: 3)\n- `WithStartingChunkSize(int)`: Set initial batch size (default: computed)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue](m)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx, WithMaxRetries(5)) {\n    process(k, v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatalf(\"Iteration failed: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n#### `BatchIterator.Err() error`\n\nReturns any error encountered during the previous `IterateAll()` call.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Error is reset when `IterateAll()` is called again\n- Reusing the iterator resets the error\n\n#### Helper Functions\n\n`CountAll[KT, VT, KP, VP](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error)`\n\nCounts all entries using the batch iterator.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\n### Pinning Concepts\n\n**Pinned maps** are persisted to the BPF filesystem and survive process restarts. **Unpinned maps** exist only in kernel memory and are destroyed when the process exits.\n\n### Pin/Unpin Operations\n\n#### `Unpin() error`\n\nUnpins (removes) the map from the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes the pinned map file\n- The map remains open and functional until explicitly closed\n- The next process loading the map will create a new one\n\n#### `UnpinIfExists() error`\n\nUnpins the map only if it exists, returning no error if it doesn't.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if map exists first\n- Returns nil if map doesn't exist\n- Otherwise identical to Unpin()\n\n### BPF Filesystem Paths\n\n#### `BPFFSRoot() string`\n\nReturns the root path where the BPF filesystem is mounted (typically `/sys/fs/bpf`).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns the global bpffsRoot path\n- Locked after first access to prevent misconfiguration\n\n#### `CiliumPath() string`\n\nReturns the BPF filesystem path for Cilium object pins (typically `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium`).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns filepath joined with BPFFSRoot\n- Locked after first access\n\n#### `MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string`\n\nReturns the filesystem path where a map with the given name will be pinned.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Differs based on component (Cilium agent vs others)\n- For Cilium agent: returns path in TCGlobalsPath\n- For others: derives path from mount info\n\n#### `TCGlobalsPath() string`\n\nReturns the legacy TC globals path for map pins (typically `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals`).\n\n#### `LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string`\n\nReturns a name for a map that is local to a specific ID.\n\n**Format:** `{name}{id:05d}` (zero-padded 5-digit ID)\n\n#### `LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string`\n\nReturns the filesystem path for a locally-scoped map.\n\n### Map Persistence Behavior\n\n**OpenOrCreate() behavior:**\n- Pinned maps (default): Loads from pin path if compatible, recreates if incompatible\n- Non-persistent maps: Always recreates, ignoring any existing pin\n- Map spec Pinning flag: Determines if map is pinned during creation\n\n**CreateUnpinned() behavior:**\n- Creates map without pinning (exists only in memory)\n- Useful for temporary maps\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\n### MapKey Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapKey instance.\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String() string` (via Stringer)\n- `New()` must return a fresh pointer instance\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        [16]byte\n    Family    uint8\n    Key       uint8\n    ClusterID uint16\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"IP:%v, Family:%d\", k.IP, k.Family)\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapValue instance.\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String() string`\n- `New()` must return a fresh pointer instance\n\n### MapPerCPUValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n\n    // NewSlice must return a pointer to a slice of structs implementing MapValue.\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\n**Additional Requirement:**\n- `NewSlice()` returns a pointer to a slice containing MapValue instances (one per CPU)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyValue struct {\n    Counter uint64\n}\n\ntype MyValueSlice []MyValue\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"counter=%d\", v.Counter)\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &MyValue{}\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) NewSlice() any {\n    s := make(MyValueSlice, 0)\n    return &s\n}\n```\n\n### EndpointKey Example\n\nEndpointKey is a concrete example implementing MapKey:\n\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6\n    Family    uint8\n    Key       uint8\n    ClusterID uint16\n}\n\n// Supports both IPv4 (in lowest 4 bytes) and IPv6\n// Family: 1 for IPv4, 2 for IPv6\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string {\n    // Returns string representation like \"10.0.0.1:0\"\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n\nfunc NewEndpointKey(addr netip.Addr, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey {\n    // Auto-detects address family and constructs key\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\nEvents provide a way to track map modifications in real-time without polling. Maps record update, delete, and bulk-delete operations to a bounded circular buffer.\n\n### Event Types\n\n#### Action Enum\n\n```go\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate  Action = iota  // Single entry updated\n    MapDelete                  // Single entry deleted\n    MapDeleteAll               // Bulk delete (aggregated)\n)\n```\n\n#### Event Struct\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp time.Time  // When the event occurred\n    // Contains Action, Key, Value, DesiredAction, LastError fields\n}\n```\n\n**Methods:**\n- `GetAction() string`: Returns action as string (\"update\", \"delete\", \"delete-all\")\n- `GetKey() string`: Returns string representation of key\n- `GetValue() string`: Returns string representation of value\n- `GetLastError() error`: Returns last error (for failed operations)\n- `GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction`: Returns desired action enum\n\n### Event Subscription\n\n#### `DumpAndSubscribe(ctx context.Context, callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool)`\n\nDumps existing events and optionally subscribes to future events.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for controlling subscription lifetime\n- `callback`: Function called for each event\n- `follow`: If true, continues receiving new events after dump\n\n**Type Definition:**\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(Event)\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- First calls callback for all existing events in buffer\n- If follow=true, subscribes to future events via stream\n- Subscription ends when context is cancelled\n- Events in buffer are filtered by TTL (expired events excluded)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"%s: %s -> %s\\n\", e.GetAction(), e.GetKey(), e.GetValue())\n}, true)\n\n// Later...\ncancel() // Stop receiving events\n```\n\n#### `IsEventsEnabled() bool`\n\nReturns whether the event buffer is enabled for this map.\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n#### `WithEvents(config option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map`\n\nEnables event buffering on the map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `config.Enabled`: Whether to enable event buffer\n- `config.MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to buffer\n- `config.TTL`: How long to keep events (0 = keep forever)\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates a bounded circular buffer for events\n- Automatically garbage collects expired events if TTL > 0\n- Uses approximately 100MB per million capacity\n- Returns immediately if Enabled=false\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, key, value, 10000, 0).\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 10000,\n        TTL:     5 * time.Minute,\n    }).\n    OpenOrCreate()\n```\n\n### DesiredAction Enum\n\n```go\ntype DesiredAction uint8\n\nconst (\n    OK     DesiredAction = iota  // Entry is in sync\n    Insert                        // Entry needs to be created/updated\n    Delete                        // Entry needs to be deleted\n)\n```\n\n**Used by:** Cache and event system to track synchronization state\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nThe collection loading system handles loading eBPF programs and maps from ELF files compiled with eBPF C code.\n\n### Collection Loading Functions\n\n#### `LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)`\n\nLoads an eBPF collection and assigns it to the provided struct.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for debug output\n- `to`: Target struct to assign loaded objects to (typically contains *Map fields)\n- `spec`: The compiled eBPF collection specification\n- `opts`: Load options\n\n**Returns:**\n- Commit function: must be called after attaching programs to hooks\n- Error: if loading failed\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Analyzes struct fields to determine which objects to keep\n- Loads the collection into the kernel\n- Assigns maps and programs to matching struct fields\n- Returns a commit function for finalizing pins\n\n**Commit Function:**\n- Must be called after all programs are attached to their hooks\n- Commits any map pins that were marked for replacement\n- When multiple programs from same ELF are attached, call commit only after all are attached\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype Objects struct {\n    Map1 *bpf.Map `ebpf:\"map_name_1\"`\n    Map2 *bpf.Map `ebpf:\"map_name_2\"`\n    Prog *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"xdp_prog\"`\n}\n\nspec, err := ebpf.LoadCollectionSpec(\"program.o\")\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\nobj := &Objects{}\ncommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(logger, obj, spec, nil)\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Attach programs...\nerr = syscall.BpfProgAttach(...)\n\n// After all programs attached:\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n#### `LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)`\n\nLoads a collection into the kernel.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for debug output\n- `spec`: The compiled eBPF collection specification\n- `opts`: Load options\n\n**Returns:**\n- Collection: loaded maps and programs\n- Commit function: must be called after attaching programs\n- Error: if loading failed\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Validates all programs have specified types\n- Renames maps according to opts.MapRenames\n- Applies runtime constant overrides\n- Computes reachability and removes unused programs\n- Resolves tail calls\n- Removes unused maps\n- Handles map pinning and compatibility checks\n- Returns commit function for replacing pins\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Replacements for datapath runtime configs (DECLARE_CONFIG)\n    Constants any\n\n    // Maps to be renamed during loading\n    // Key is key in CollectionSpec.Maps, value is new name\n    MapRenames []map[string]string\n\n    // Maps to be replaced with existing Map instances\n    // Used to replace maps with pre-configured ones\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n\n    // Set of objects to keep during reachability pruning\n    Keep *set.Set[string]\n\n    // Path to write constants dump for debugging\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n```\n\n**Constants Field:**\n- Pass a pointer to a populated struct from pkg/datapath/config\n- Used to override runtime-configurable values in eBPF code\n\n**MapRenames Field:**\n- Array of rename maps for flexibility\n- Later renames override earlier ones\n- Used to give maps unique names based on context\n\n**MapReplacements Field:**\n- Replace specific maps with pre-existing Map instances\n- Maps are specified by their CollectionSpec name\n- Useful for reusing maps across program loads\n\n### Pinning Behavior\n\n**Automatic Pinning:**\n- Maps marked as pinned in the spec are automatically loaded from opts.Maps.PinPath\n- Maps with incompatible existing pins are re-created and re-pinned\n- Maps with CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE flag have their pins replaced via commit function\n\n**Pin Replacement:**\n- Maps are not re-pinned immediately after loading\n- The returned commit function handles pin replacement\n- This allows multiple programs from same ELF to be attached before finalizing\n\n**Reasons for Pin Replacement:**\n1. Map incompatibility after upgrades/downgrades\n2. Tail call maps should not be repopulated with stale programs\n3. Maps with CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE flag set\n\n### Map Compatibility\n\nWhen opening a pinned map, Cilium checks:\n- Key size\n- Value size\n- Map type\n- Maximum entries\n- Flags\n\nIf any property differs, the map is considered incompatible and will be replaced.\n\n### Constants and Configuration\n\nRuntime configuration values can be defined in eBPF code using `DECLARE_CONFIG()` and overridden during loading:\n\n```go\nopts := &CollectionOptions{\n    Constants: &datapath.Config{\n        LBMapSize: 100000,\n        TupleSize: 48,\n    },\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Cache and Synchronization\n\n### Map Caching\n\nMaps can maintain a local cache of entries and track their synchronization state with the kernel.\n\n#### `WithCache() *Map`\n\nEnables caching on the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Stores all user-space inserted entries in a local cache\n- Tracks each entry's synchronization state (Insert, Delete, OK)\n- Automatically schedules error resolver if insertion fails\n- Enables periodic reconciliation of failed operations\n\n**Use Case:** When you need to track which operations failed and retry them\n\n### Pressure Metrics\n\n#### `WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map`\n\nEnables tracking of map pressure (utilization).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Tracks map fill ratio as a metric\n- Reported only if over threshold (0.0 by default)\n- Metric updated with each map operation\n\n#### `WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map`\n\nEnables pressure metric with custom threshold.\n\n**Threshold:** Metric is only reported if pressure >= threshold\n\n### Builder Pattern\n\nAll `With*` methods return the Map instance, enabling fluent configuration:\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"name\", mapType, key, value, size, flags).\n    WithCache().\n    WithPressureMetric(registry).\n    WithEvents(config).\n    OpenOrCreate()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Utility Functions\n\n### Map Information\n\n#### `Name() string`\n\nReturns the basename of the map.\n\n#### `Path() (string, error)`\n\nReturns the filesystem path where the map is or will be pinned.\n\n#### `FD() int`\n\nReturns the file descriptor of the kernel map object.\n\n#### `IsOpen() bool`\n\nReturns whether the map is currently open.\n\n#### `Type() ebpf.MapType`\n\nReturns the map type (Hash, Array, etc.).\n\n#### `KeySize() uint32`\n\nReturns the size of key in bytes.\n\n#### `ValueSize() uint32`\n\nReturns the size of value in bytes.\n\n#### `MaxEntries() uint32`\n\nReturns the maximum number of entries.\n\n#### `Flags() uint32`\n\nReturns the creation flags.\n\n### Model Export\n\n#### `GetModel() *models.BPFMap`\n\nReturns an API model representation of the map for debugging/monitoring.\n\n**Includes:**\n- Map path\n- Cache entries (if cache enabled)\n- Key and value strings\n- Desired actions\n- Last error information\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Types\n\n**ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist:** Key not found in map (from ebpf-go)\n\n**ebpf.ErrMapIncompatible:** Map incompatible with existing pin (from ebpf-go)\n\n**unix.ENOSPC:** Buffer too small for batch operation (batch iterator auto-retries)\n\n**ErrMapNotOpened:** Map not opened yet (used by map ops)\n\n**ErrMaxLookup:** Iteration limit exceeded (unreliable iteration)\n\n### Error Resolver\n\nWhen caching is enabled, maps automatically schedule an error resolver that:\n- Runs periodically to reconcile cache and kernel state\n- Retries failed insertions\n- Retries failed deletions\n- Backs off exponentially with minimum 5-second intervals\n- Stops when all errors are resolved\n\n---\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Map Creation:** Always pin maps for persistence across restarts\n2. **Error Handling:** Check for `ErrKeyNotExist` separately from other errors\n3. **Iteration:** Use `BatchIterator` for large maps for better performance\n4. **Concurrency:** Map operations are thread-safe but hold locks - keep callbacks short\n5. **Event Subscription:** Always cancel context to avoid resource leaks\n6. **Lock Awareness:** Never call `Delete()` from DumpCallback; use `DeleteLocked()`\n7. **Collection Loading:** Always call the commit function after attaching programs\n8. **Cleanup:** Close maps when done to release kernel resources\n9. **Testing:** Use `PrivilegedTest` and `CheckOrMountFS` for unit tests\n10. **Per-CPU Maps:** Verify value type implements `MapPerCPUValue` before iteration\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"
}
